<Review>Wayy too overpriced for the same bland food. A pound of cantaloupe sets you back almost 7 dollars, and they purposefully overweigh it by adding a heavier plate. Menus never change for the restraunts, so after a couple weeks of eating chicken tenders and fries every day you might understand why UC students hate the Pavillion. But yeah, let's let the chancellor walk away with 6 figures.

Edit 1- UCM moved from meal plan to meal swipes. I am no longer a regular, as I live off campus now, but have paid the crazy 18$ dinner fee a few times when I was not in the mood to cook or drive somewhere. The food is the same boring stuff, although I have heard that there have been some good items on the menu occasionally. They added curly fries every once in a while, which were very good, for what they were.

At the end of the day still not worth it at all to me, but if you have nothing else, it's there. And you can eat as much as you want. Beats the scam that is the Los Reyes food truck.</Review><Gmap_id>0x80914747c33c69d9:0xd0b2b47a49cf593c<//Gmap_id><rating>1< /rating>< date>

<Gmap_id>0x80c2bbe3e14a04bf:0x1af88e2dc98857d0< /Gmap_id><Text>We came here for dinner on a Saturday night, so it was fairly crowded and noisy. The food was well-meaning, but definitely on the pricier side.

We started with the radicchio salad. Toss radicchio, which is inherently more of a bitter leaf, with a healthy dose of strong parmesan and an anchovy vinaigrette and you get a salty, bitter salad. They would do well to finish the salad with a sprinkle of caramelized lemon juice to balance the bitter with sweet. Along with the salad we got the chickpea panelle, which was definitely a winner. Fried diamonds of chickpea flour batter, again with a grating of parmesan and lemon wedges on the side made this dish especially curious for us, as we had never seen chickpea flour used outside of Indian cuisine! Not sure if they do this for all guests, but they provided us with a recipe card at the end of our meal!

The main entrees we got were the rigatoni pasta and the funghi pizza. The chicken liver ragu on the pasta had an earthy, herby sweetness to it that hit the right notes, and the rigatoni was cooked well with a strong bite. Since I almost always order a tomato-based pizza at restaurants, we opted for the mushroom pizza. It had a garlicky mushroom cream base and a sturdy-yet soft crust which beckoned the "folding" pizza handling technique. About that, the crust was soft and chewy. Not the most ideal crust IMO because there wasn't much of a crunch to the bite, but to each his/her own. It's got the signature char marks and carries the pie well, so it's a keeper. I can't speak much to the mushrooms other than saying there was a good variety. I would be remiss, however, to leave out the scamorza really pulling through with the sharp smoky goodness. to complement the meaty mushroom flavor. Who says you need meat to get great flavor??</Text><response>None< /response>< time>

< user>
104846396872416803360</user>
<username>Norman Anderson</username><time>1453460841079</time><rating>4< /rating>< Review>
Chose Sotto for a holiday dinner with a friend and was happy with the choice.  Located underground the popular Peruvian restaurant Picca, Sotto is a dark, cool, hipster-chic space.  Furnished handsomely in dark wood and draped in dim lighting, the space feels hip and modern while retaining a rustic air.

I couldn't choose between 3 pastas and a pizza, so we got all of them -- happy holidays to me!  The spread consisted of the Paccheri, Rigatoni, Squie Ink Mafaldine, and the Guanciale Pizza.  I really appreciated our waiter, who was more than knowledgeable about the entire menu (both food and wine) and took his time walking us through the various options and their merits.  He was really sweet on top of it all, so I was won over before the food reached the table.

My favorites in order from most favorite to least are the Rigatoni, Paccheri, Guanciale, and the Squid Ink Mafaldine. The Rigatoni came with chicken liver ragu, maitake mushrooms, and grana cheese.  This is a very earthy dish, with a lot of deep flavors coming from the rich chicken livers and the mushrooms.  I personally love this flavor profile and this dish was an instant hit.

The Paccheri is a wide tube pasta that came with sweet and spicy pork ragu, rapini, and fennel pollen.  Let it be noted here that all of the pastas of the night came perfectly al dente and were quite lovely.  The paccheri noodle in particular was very nice -- the wide tube pasta held the flavorful ragu well and it was a cohesive and complete dish.

The Guanciale pizza came topped with house-cured pork cheek, ricotta, scallions, and fennel pollen.  My favorite part of Sotto's pizza is definitely the dough -- soft and chewy with just the right amount of elasticity. I ate every last bite of crust, believe me.  Other than that, the pork had good caramelization - although I wish there was more of it - and I couldn't help but want some sort of light saucing, as the pizza ate a bit dry.

Finally, the Squid Ink Mafaldine was probably the most disappointing dish for me, only because I had the highest hopes for it walking in.  Although there was good textural contrast from the crunchy breadcrumbs and the creamy burrata, the sauce was overwhelmingly acidic and tasted more of pungent tomato than anything.  It wasn't what I was expecting and, unfortunately, I wasn't completely sold.

Overall, I really enjoyed my meal at Sotto.  The ambiance along with the great service and pastas made me a very happy camper and I don't doubt that I will be back in the future.< /Review>

<user>111219392552829619639</user>< user_name>
Patrick Leyden<//user_name>
<Date>1575178286477</Date><rating>4< /rating>< review>
It's very crowded if you choose to visit during the summer, so plan accordingly. They like to say it all expenses paid but when read over the fine print you find out you paid extra for that package. The food is pretty good during your stay but you quickly realize that the decent variety of food was average at best after you leave. The lines at the restaurants and barbershops are extremely long but they go quicker than expected. Haircut options are very limited but you can upgrade your package with more options at no extra cost the longer you stay. A positive is the bedrooms are massive but the negative is you'll have to share with quite a few roommates. By far the best thing here is the fitness program. The staff are very motivated to constantly keep improving your physical fitness levels. They won't let you give up, they'll even provide extra individual workouts for you if you desire. The staff were a little to motivated for me. For some reason they felt like they had to yell all the time and they expect you to do the same, so that was kinda annoying. Overall my stay was more enjoyable than average. I originally gave a 3‚≠ê rating but while writing I realized it my stay was quite a bit better than my current stay, in Oceanside.< /review>

<rate>5< /rate><Review>I stepped on these pair of yellow footprints here back in 1997...
I was met by a really excited, well dressed man who said his name was sir.  I think that might have been his last name and his first name might have been  Isaac or something because we all said I- Sir any time we spoke to him.

I stayed here for about 13 weeks, the mail service is spectacular but theres no wifi which I was disappointed. My room was very clean, i mean VERY clean but I had to share it with about 65 other males.

The wake up service was prompt and very loud, but very efficient.

We were assigned a guide who took us to various parts of the property. They have strict standards so when our original was not up to parr, he was quickly replaced.

This was an all inclusive property so we enjoyed three very nice meals a day but I guess I didnt get the all inclusive drink package because there was no soda and no alcoholic beverages all though I had all the water I could drink and it came in a cool green canteen.  I guess they are very water conscious and didnt want to waste any because at the end of the night we had to drink our entire canteen and then hold it out above our heads.

The gym here is FANTASIC, great athletic director.  They have a very elaborate adult jungle gym. For more of a botique style environment they have a small area that is part exercise facility, part exfoliation called the Sand Pit.  I spent many many hours here, again with several of my very enthusiastic nicely dressed hosts.

They also have a great offsite shooting range.

If you are staying here for a while I highly recommend the hiking trail called The Grim Reaper, lovely views and a very memorable experience.

For anyone still reading this review I highly recommend coming here and trying it out for yourself. It is sure to be a very memorable experience.  You will probably, like me, spend the rest of your life reminiscing about your stay here.

Plt 1065 1997</Review>< pics>

<Resp>None< /Resp>< text>
I took some time off a while back and booked a stay at this resort for about 13 weeks. I wasn't sure what to expect, but I figured "what the heck?" To my pleasant surprise, this place was amazing!

The other people staying at this resort were friendly and most of us got along well. I slept in a building with an open floor plan that accommodated quite a few people. The only complaint I have is the bathroom situation can be a little hectic. Also, sometimes tornadoes would blow through and mess up the furniture, so be prepared for that.

The food was so delicious, I don't think it took me longer than a couple of minutes to eat it. I felt like such a pig, but what's the fun of a vacation if you have to watch what you eat? Plus, it's almost a shame to sit inside stuffing your face when you could be outside mingling with your friends and trying to get the full experience of this depot!

From the time I woke up until the time I finally went to sleep, there were tons of activities to do. There was never a dull moment. Also, the staff here are extremely courteous and helpful and will never let you doubt yourself. They will always help you find a way to conquer whatever it is you are doing that day.

If I have to say something bad about this place, which is only fair in a review, I would say the proximity to the airport is a little annoying. Sometimes the jets taking off would keep me awake and it always made me sad knowing people were leaving San Diego without ever knowing this gem of a depot existed.

When it was finally time to leave, which came WAY too quickly, I was sad to see this place go. From all of the staff and people I became good friends with to the beautiful interior and exterior design, I just couldn't stand the thought of waking up somewhere else. Alas, all good things must come to an end.

I HIGHLY recommend this place, but make sure you book 13 weeks so you can experience everything this place has to offer. Anything less than that and you aren't doing yourself justice.< /text>

< text>
I had a great time here. Lots of exercise, sunny, very close to lots of great places, and interesting food opportunities. I remember during our off hours, some recruits would hang out at the "food court" and eat.

Some would quibble over terms and say a more accurate portrayal would be sneaking out at night and scavenging MRE components from dumpsters and hiding them in their footlockers, Private Pyle Style, but they just don't know how to look on the bright side of life. Plus, all the food smuggled in wasn't just from dumpsters.

One recruit had his wife bring in a bunch of candy to the Mormon Sunday service, and several recruits joined him in hiding it under their cammies to sneak it back into the squad bay, where they recruit-taped it to the tops of the pipes above the showers. That was the best candy we ever had, let me tell you.

One lucky recruit even found some week-old Claim Jumpers leftovers that had just been thrown away one night, and got himself a nice Claim Jumpers meal, even if he did litter the head with the containers for the drill instructors to find the next morning. Despite the best efforts of the drill instructors, we never did find out who the lucky winner of the trash-digging contest was, though we all had our suspicions. While I could go on all day about the lovely food, there were plenty of other high points.

Though a few poor sports did break the rules about turning in everything on arrival including the most basic common sense, by and large, most people went along with it. There were plenty of fun events they hosted here such as the Improvise Toilet Paper Challenge, the Drill Instructor Shuffle, and the Bladder Control Failure March. In the end, I think the old motto sums the place up the best. San Diego Recruit Depot: Where Civilians Become Mentally Challenged Recruits.</text>

< text>
What a terrible place to stay.  First off, you can't book a room without a three month commitment.  The hairstylists only know one style.  The staff steal your clothes and replace them with an outfit that looks like a computer threw up all over it. The food is free but absolutely terrible.  The locals are loud and don't know the meaning of personal space, in fact even the building designers neglected to incorporate any sort of private areas.  You get dust and sand everywhere and hardly any sleep.  There hasn't been any money spent soundproofing the place from the constant air traffic next door.  While I left thirty pounds lighter and overly patriotic, I can't recommend this resort with anything higher than one star.</text>

< Time>
1542208529625</Time>
< username>
Josh Lumley</username>
<Review>Some places may offer discount vacations, others might even offer a free vacation, but to my knowledge this is the only place that will actually pay you to take a 3 month vacation free of charge. Once there, you'll receive a number of other free amenities including free meals, free water (although it's kind of yellow), free haircuts (although they seem rushed and way too close), 1-3 free phone calls and free personal trainers. But wait, there's more. While vacationing at "The Depot" you'll get free lessons in marching, shooting, martial arts and pugil sticks.

The amenities are rather sparse, but it's all part of the experience. While the mattresses are thin and the pillows are barely there, I never had an issue going to sleep in under 5 minutes. They have community showers and insist you use them each day, although sometimes only one shower head is allowed to be used. The restrooms were always spotless, even if they were missing the doors. Still, I found it quite nice some days to use the facilities while having a quaint conversation with one of my new found friends.

I would however avoid the sand pit, or that rather small piece of linoleum known as the quarter deck (which was odd because I never found any quarters there, even with my face pressed against it.) The personal trainers can be a bit up tight, but their routines are often filled with some of the best comedic material I've ever heard, although, I will warn you they're not very good at taking a compliment. Every time I laughed at one of their jokes, it was not received well, although I did usually win a trip to the pit, but it wasn't my cup of tea, although you may like it.

One negative is that there are zero women here. In fact, you most likely will not see a single woman until the end of your 13 week stay. Which I think accounts for some of my fellow travelers marrying very large women after leaving.

Finally, at the end of all, they give you a huge sendoff, beginning with each of you--who are still there--receiving a small token of achievement known as an "EGA". My ceremony was attended by a movie star, R. Lee Ermey, and was a spectacular moment, even if there seemed to have been some onion ninjas who seem to have ambushed a good number of my new friends. Then on the last day, they have a whole parade in your honor and invite your family, many of whom no longer recognize their sons.

While I had mixed emotions about my trip when I left there in 1998, I cannot recommend it highly enough today.<//Review><Rating>5</Rating><Response>None< /Response>< GmapID>
0x80deaba419e6d5b5:0x991353ac0955b5de<//GmapID>
</record>

Came here to try out their taco Tuesday dollar special, since we already have multiple places already have similar deals. < Rating>
5</Rating>
<text>$1 tacos on Tuesdays but only on the meat tacos (seafood and potato tacos excluded).

Came here wanting to try the burritos after seeing photos and good reviews but opted for tacos instead because it was tuesday. The normal prices are probably a bit high, but a solid deal on tuesdays.

As the reviews have already mentioned the real star of this place are the different salsas available. Mixing and matching the 3 are the best way to go here. I like the habanero sauce for a little heat but prefer the other two for flavor.

Definitely give this a shot if you're in the area, but there are plenty of great taco choices in LA so I can't say it's one of my top 5.<//text><Pics>None< /Pics><resp>None<//resp><GmapID>0x80c2c4de38e69b71:0xabb98531c114133d</GmapID></record></dataset><record>

<UserId.>103049127116529259560< /UserId.><Name>Chi Yu< /Name><time>1595740265360</time>< Rating>
5< /Rating>
< text>
This is my go-to taco place. I absolutely love their street-style tacos and salsas. The meats might be a bit on the dry side but that's what salsa is for. I usually order the crunchy potato, grilled fish, carnitas, asada, and pastor. They indulge my overly greedy requests for their salsas and pico de gallo (they ask how many of each when you order). Even if you're into spicy, don't pass over the mild salsa. The mild is smokey and packed full of flavor, so be sure to get mild with your medium and hot. This place has gotten got very popular, even though they canceled $1 Taco Tuesdays WAAH, so I suggest ordering ahead by phone. The service is always friendly and usually spot-on. They short-changed my order once, but they made it right without issue, and made sure the missed items were ready for me when I returned.< /text>

<Rate>5<//Rate>< text>
I'd recommend calling ahead to order (and not using a money sucking 3rd party service) because the service can be slow and seemingly out of order, but the food hasn't disappointed yet. It's a unique style as the name might suggest, so don't come straight from Roberto's/Alberto's/Hilberto's and expect the same thing. Tacos, burritos, tortas, and burritos are all delicious. Fish really sticks out, but all the meats are done well and I like that the carne asada isn't mostly chunks of fat like other places.
Also, if you get an itching for a burger, the Spanglish Burger is bomb.</text>

<Text>Have heard good things about this place and was driving by so decided to stop.

Ordered the asada nachos and was underwhelmed. The good: the chips were good quality and held their crunch under the cheese. The bad: the meat was overcooked so was dry and they give you a small portion. They don't give you guacamole in the nachos, that's blasphemy lol. A bit greasy and while I understand they're nachos and melted cheese I should not have a small pool of grease at the end.

Also ordered 2 fish tacos, one soft and one hard shell. The shrimp was under seasoned and do yourself a favor and get the hard shell.

<text>Geezuz this is a Mexican oasis ... I tried 3 different tacos the asada (beef), the pastor (pork) and the chorrizo (sausage).

All the meats were absolutely delicious and flavorful from being marinated; each taco comes with onions and cilantro served on a very fresh corn tortilla. The sauces are extra but not a complaint. I highly recommend having them grill jalapeno peppers (each whole one is $0.50). Ask them and they will cut them up. They make an excellent addition to the taco.

They also offer a very diverse menu. Sure it's a little more expensive than a run-of-the-mill taco truck or a Chipotle's but you definitely get what you pay for in terms of quality and taste. This is a place worth coming back to many times over just to taste their menu.

Everything is made with very high quality and the people working there are exceptionally friendly. It's a busy place and once you taste the food you'll know why.< /text><Pics>None</Pics>< Resp>

We do avoid it on Tuesday though because they have taco Tuesdays and they have $1 tacos which is a great deal but there servings tend to be a bit smaller on Tuesdays. Another thing is the sauces...my boyfriend and I love the habanero sauce and the red sauce...but we ask for 6 at a time because they put such a small amount in each container..so 3 equals to one. But we do love the food here...we recommend it to anyone who wants good Mexican fast food! We will definitely keep going back!<//text>

< text>
It is obvious to anyone paying attention that Americans have an obsession with Mexican food especially in L.A. So what Spanglish Kitchen has to offer? They offer simple, delicoso and authentic Mexican food. It is located in a little plaza on the corner of Atlantic Blvd and Alhambra Rd. We had Tortas and Asada Burrito with chips. The meats are fresh, juicy and soft for your mouth to devour. Staff are very friendly and competent. Similarly, their service is fast. Prices are relatively $ fair. They have outdoor seating only. Parking is very limited. In our humble opinion, Spanglish Kitchen is a great place to grab food. Definitely we'll be back!! Luckily we live just down the road. #SpanglishKitchen</text>
